ARTICLE HIGHLIGHTS: The extent to which partitioned polygenic risk scores (pPRS) for type 2 diabetes influence the relationship between insulin secretion and sensitivity has not been examined in people with prediabetes. We investigated whether insulin secretion compensation and demand, estimated through the relationship between insulin secretion and sensitivity, mediated or modified the associations of two sets of pPRS with diabetes incidence in Diabetes Prevention Program participants. Several pPRS modified the effects of insulin demand on diabetes incidence, but none modified the effect of compensation. In people with prediabetes, inadequate compensatory insulin secretion contributes to progression to diabetes regardless of genetic risk as measured by pPRS.

## 抗老化 Reserve-19. Prevalence of frailty, multimorbidity, and polypharmacy and their association with health outcomes in hospitalized older adults: a prospective multicenter cohort study.

- Candidate bucket: Reserve
- 事前スコア: 5
- PMID: 42365277
- DOI: 10.1186/s12877-026-07889-7
- Journal: BMC geriatrics
- PubDate: 2026-06-27
- PublicationType: Journal Article
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42365277/
- OA URL: https://doi.org/10.1186/s12877-026-07889-7
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
BACKGROUND: The growing burden of frailty, multimorbidity, and polypharmacy among older adults presents major challenges to healthcare systems worldwide. These interrelated conditions are known to worsen clinical outcomes, yet data from the region are limited. This study aimed to examine the prevalence and clinical impact of frailty, complex multimorbidity, and polypharmacy among hospitalized older adults in Oman.
METHODS: A prospective, multicenter cohort study was conducted in general internal medicine wards of two tertiary hospitals in Oman. Patients aged ≥ 65 years were consecutively enrolled and assessed for frailty using Clinical Frailty Scale (CFS), multimorbidity using the Charlson Comorbidity Index (CCI) and a definition of complex multimorbidity (≥ 3 chronic conditions), and polypharmacy (≥ 5 medications). Clinical outcomes included hospital length of stay (LOS), in-hospital mortality, HD/ICU admission, 30- and 90-day mortality, and 30- and 90-day readmission. Multivariable regression and Kaplan-Meier survival analyses were used.
RESULTS: Among 369 patients, high frailty, complex multimorbidity, and polypharmacy were present in 139 (37.67%), 126 (34.15%), and 243 (65.85%) patients, respectively. Higher frailty was associated with longer LOS (6.49 vs. 4.88 days, p < 0.01) and increased in-hospital mortality (15.11% vs. 3.54%, p < 0.01). High frailty independently predicted 30-day mortality (adjusted odds ratio [aOR] 5.68, p < 0.01) and 90-day mortality (aOR 3.53, p < 0.01). Complex multimorbidity independently predicted 30-day readmission (aOR 1.92, p = 0.015), 30-day mortality (aOR 2.12, p = 0.026), and 90-day mortality (aOR 2.42, p < 0.01). Kaplan-Meier and adjusted Cox regression analyses showed lower 90-day survival and higher mortality risk among patients with high frailty (adjusted hazard ratio [aHR] 3.16, 95% CI 1.69-5.89, p < 0.001) and complex multimorbidity (aHR 1.85, 95% CI 1.15-2.98, p = 0.011).
CONCLUSION: Frailty, complex multimorbidity, and polypharmacy were common among hospitalized older adults in Oman. High frailty and complex multimorbidity were the most consistent predictors of adverse outcomes, supporting early recognition, structured geriatric assessment pathways, and future targeted patient-centered interventions.

Regular physical activity is known to have multiple benefits in general aging population, but its specific benefits for those with HIV are less established.
AIM: This review assessed randomized controlled trials (RCTs) investigating the effects of physical exercise on quality of life, VO₂ max, and sleep quality among seniors with HIV.
METHODS: A systematic search was conducted in PubMed, CINAHL, Cochrane Library, and Embase. Eligible studies included RCTs evaluating structured exercise interventions in adults aged 50 years and older living with HIV. Data on participants, interventions, and outcomes were extracted and pooled for meta-analysis.
RESULTS: Ten RCTs involving 372 participants met the inclusion criteria. Participants had lived with HIV for 9-25 years. Exercise interventions were associated with significant improvements in quality of life (p < 0.01, Z = 7.16, I² = 70%) and VO₂ max (p < 0.05, Z = 1.99, I² = 88%). However, no significant effect was observed on sleep quality (p ˃ 0.05, Z = 0.16, I² = 79%).
CONCLUSION: This systematic review and meta-analysis indicate that physical activity can enhance quality of life and aerobic capacity among older adults living with HIV, although benefits for sleep quality were not demonstrated. These findings highlight the value of incorporating exercise into routine care for this population. Further large-scale, high-quality RCTs are recommended to confirm these outcomes and explore long-term effects.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Core-1. The Effects of Glucagon-Like Peptide-1 Receptor Agonists and Sodium-Glucose Co-Transporter-2 Inhibitors on Lean Body Mass in Humans: A Systematic Review and Meta-Analysis of Randomised Controlled Trials.

- Candidate bucket: Core
- 事前スコア: 27
- PMID: 42319968
- DOI: 10.1002/dmrr.70194
- Journal: Diabetes/metabolism research and reviews
- PubDate: 2026-07-01
- PublicationType: Systematic Review; Journal Article; Meta-Analysis; Review
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42319968/
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
AIMS: The use of pharmacotherapies with weight loss properties for the management of obesity and chronic disease are now routinely prescribed. We investigated the evidence from randomised-controlled trials for the effects on lean body mass of glucagon-like peptide-1 receptor agonists (GLP-1RA) and sodium-glucose co-transporter-2 inhibitors (SGLT2i) in humans.
MATERIALS AND METHODS: PubMed, MEDLINE, the Cochrane Library and CINAHL were searched from inception to October 2022. The primary outcome was change in body composition focused on measures of lean body mass (LBM).
RESULTS: Thirty-six studies in population groups with obesity (n = 8), type 2 diabetes mellitus (n = 20), type 1 diabetes mellitus (n = 5) and polycystic ovary syndrome (n = 3) receiving a GLP-1RA or SGLT2i therapy versus placebo or active comparator satisfied our inclusion criteria, including 21 for GLP-1RA and 15 for SGLT2i. Meta-analysis showed an overall loss of LBM in the direction of the intervention groups prescribed GLP-1RA (MD: -1.51 kg [95% CI: -2.00 to -1.01]) and SGLT2i (MD: -1.04 kg [95% CI: -1.45 to -0.64]) with sub-group analysis showing largely consistent results when stratified by type of body composition outcome, type of body composition measurement technique and disease status. Results were not modified by sex. Further meta-analysis found that lean mass accounted for 28% (95% CI: 22%-34%) of overall weight loss induced by GLP-1RA and SGLT2i.
CONCLUSIONS: GLP-1RA and SGLT2i are associated with a loss of LBM that appears congruent with overall weight loss. Monitoring of body composition and provision of combined therapy to preserve lean mass during weight loss should be considered.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Core-2. Effectiveness of Whole-Body Vibration Therapy on Handgrip Strength: A Systematic Review and Meta-Analysis of Randomized Controlled Trials.

- Candidate bucket: Core
- 事前スコア: 20
- PMID: 42373946
- DOI: 10.1002/msc.70246
- Journal: Musculoskeletal care
- PubDate: 2026-09-01
- PublicationType: Journal Article; Systematic Review; Meta-Analysis; Review; Research Support, Non-U.S. Gov't
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42373946/
- OA URL: https://doi.org/10.1002/msc.70246
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
INTRODUCTION: Although whole-body vibration (WBV) therapy has already demonstrated efficacy in improving lower-limb muscle strength, it is still unclear whether it has similar potential for improving handgrip strength.
OBJECTIVE: To verify the efficacy of WBV on handgrip strength.
METHODS: The search was conducted on September 5, 2025, in PubMed, Embase, CENTRAL, CINAHL, SPORTDiscus, Web of Science, LILACS, PEDro, and SciELO. Risk of bias was assessed via the PEDro scale, and certainty of evidence using GRADE. Meta-analyses were performed using the standardized mean difference (SMD) under random- or fixed-effects models according to heterogeneity levels.
RESULTS: Thirty-four studies (1272 participants) were included (32.4% had a high risk of bias). Compared with controls, acute WBV showed no significant effect on handgrip strength, with moderate-certainty evidence (SMD = 0.09, p = 0.34). Chronic WBV produced a significant but small effect, supported by very low-certainty evidence (SMD = 0.33, p = 0.01). Sensitivity analysis excluding high-risk-of-bias studies rendered the chronic effect non-significant (p = 0.07). Exploratory subgroup analyses of chronic interventions showed a significant interaction for body positioning (p = 0.02), with significant effects for direct hand contact (SMD = 0.76, p = 0.03) and static standing (SMD = 0.52, p = 0.03). Compared with resistance training, evidence was inconclusive and of very low certainty (SMD = -2.43, p = 0.25).
CONCLUSION: Chronic WBV involving direct hand contact may be associated with more pronounced effects on handgrip strength; however, these findings are exploratory, supported by very low-certainty evidence, and require confirmation by future trials.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Core-3. Effects of blood flow restriction training combined with resistance training on lower-limb strength and sport-specific performance in athletes: a systematic review and meta-analysis.

- Candidate bucket: Core
- 事前スコア: 19
- PMID: 42366542
- DOI: 10.1080/07853890.2026.2658885
- Journal: Annals of medicine
- PubDate: 2026-12
- PublicationType: Journal Article; Systematic Review; Meta-Analysis
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42366542/
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
BACKGROUND: In contemporary sports science, athletes and coaches continuously explore strategies to reduce training load and injury risk while increasing muscular strength and sport-specific performance. This meta-analysis evaluated the effects of blood flow restriction training (BFRT) combined with resistance training (RT) on lower-limb muscle strength and sport-specific performance in athletes.
METHODS: Relevant randomized controlled trials (RCTs) were systematically searched across major databases (e.g. PubMed, Web of Science, Cochrane, CNKI, Wanfang Data, and Embase) from inception until November 2024. Two independent reviewers carefully assessed the studies. Data analysis was carried out using RevMan 5.4 software, which included heterogeneity testing, meta-analysis, subgroup analysis, and assessment of publication bias.
RESULTS: Ten RCTs (181 athletes; 91 in the BFRT and RT group, 90 in the control group) were included. Outcomes determined BFRT combined with RT yielded notable enhancements in lower-limb muscle strength (SMD = 1.09, 95% CI [0.52, 1.66], < 0.05) and muscle hypertrophy (MD = 1.09, 95% CI [0.10, 2.09], < 0.05) compared to control training. However, no significant improvement in sport-specific performance was found (SMD = 0.11, 95% CI [-0.18, 0.40], = 0.46). Substantial heterogeneity was observed for strength outcomes (I = 75%), whereas low heterogeneity was observed for sport-specific performance and hypertrophy outcomes (I = 0%). No evidence of significant publication bias was detected.
CONCLUSION: BFRT combined with RT appears to provide effective augmentation of lower-limb muscle strength and hypertrophy in athletes compared to RT or conventional training alone. It may be prudent to integrate this approach systematically into training cycles to optimize physiological muscle stimulation and training outcomes, despite not directly improving sport-specific performance.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Core-4. Assessing the risk of diabetic retinopathy progression with GLP-1 receptor agonists: a systematic review and meta-analysis.

- Candidate bucket: Core
- 事前スコア: 16
- PMID: 42380920
- DOI: 10.1186/s12886-026-05036-9
- Journal: BMC ophthalmology
- PubDate: 2026-06
- PublicationType: Journal Article; Systematic Review
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42380920/
- OA URL: https://doi.org/10.1186/s12886-026-05036-9
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
BACKGROUND: Diabetic retinopathy (DR) is a significant cause of vision impairment in patients with diabetes. The impact of glucagon-like peptide-1 receptor agonists (GLP-1RAs) on the progression of DR remains unclear. This systematic review and meta-analysis aimed to evaluate the association between GLP-1RA therapy and DR progression.
METHODS: A comprehensive search of electronic databases identified 161 records, of which 11 studies met the inclusion criteria. Included studies comprised randomized controlled trials (RCTs) and retrospective cohort studies conducted in North America, Europe, and East Asia, with sample sizes ranging from 137 to 9,463 participants. The primary GLP-1RAs analyzed were albiglutide, liraglutide, semaglutide, exenatide, and dulaglutide, compared to either placebo or SGLT-2 inhibitors. The primary outcome was DR progression, assessed through pooled relative risk (RR) estimates using a random-effects model. Subgroup analyses were conducted by GLP-1RA type and geographical location. Sensitivity analyses and assessment of publication bias (via funnel plot, Egger's test, and Begg's test) were performed. Risk of bias was evaluated using the Cochrane tool.
RESULTS: The meta-analysis indicated no statistically significant association between GLP-1RA use and DR progression (pooled RR = 1.07, 95% confidence interval [CI]: 0.90-1.28). Subgroup analyses by GLP-1RA type and geographical location also showed no significant differences. However, semaglutide demonstrated the highest RR for DR progression in two studies (RR = 1.76 [1.11-2.79] and RR = 6.41 [0.67-61.46]), a unique finding contrasting with the overall results. Sensitivity analyses confirmed the robustness of the findings, and no publication bias was detected (P > 0.05 for Egger's and Begg's tests). Risk of bias analysis revealed a low risk across most domains.
CONCLUSION: This meta-analysis suggests that GLP-1RA therapy is not significantly associated with an increased risk of DR progression. However, heterogeneity in outcomes, particularly with semaglutide, warrants further investigation.
TRIAL REGISTRATION: PROSPERO CRD420251007882.
CLINICAL TRIAL NUMBER: Not applicable.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Core-5. Effects of cardiac rehabilitation on atrial fibrillation recurrence, mortality, hospitalization, and exercise capacity: a systematic review and meta-analysis.

Abstract:
BACKGROUND: Cardiac rehabilitation (CR) may benefit patients with atrial fibrillation (AF) in areas such as exercise capacity. However, evidence regarding its impact on AF recurrence, a key clinical outcome, remains inconsistent. METHODS: We systematically searched the Cochrane Library, PubMed, and Embase from January 1, 1980, to April 20, 2026. Two reviewers independently screened studies, extracted data, and assessed risk of bias. A total of 1,550 patients from 11 RCTs were included in the meta-analysis based on the predefined inclusion and exclusion criteria.

CONCLUSIONS: CR is associated with a reduction in AF recurrence in the overall AF population, though this benefit was not observed in the exploratory subgroup of patients post-ablation. It significantly improves exercise capacity but does not appear to affect mortality or hospitalization rates. Further high-quality randomized trials are needed to evaluate the benefits and potential risks of CR across different types of AF.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Core-6. Walking and subjective sleep quality in adults: a Bayesian three-level meta-analysis with probabilistic clinical relevance assessment and dose-response modeling.

- Candidate bucket: Core
- 事前スコア: 16
- PMID: 42375593
- DOI: 10.3389/fpubh.2026.1864607
- Journal: Frontiers in public health
- PubDate: 2026
- PublicationType: Journal Article; Meta-Analysis; Systematic Review
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42375593/
- OA URL: https://www.frontiersin.org/journals/public-health/articles/10.3389/fpubh.2026.1864607/pdf
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
OBJECTIVE: To evaluate the effect of walking on subjective sleep quality in adults using a Bayesian three-level meta-analysis and to identify moderators of treatment response.
METHODS: PubMed, Embase, the Cochrane Library, and Web of Science were searched from inception through March 2026 for randomized controlled trials (RCTs) comparing walking interventions with inactive or non-aerobic controls. Effect sizes were calculated as Hedges' g. A Bayesian three-level random-effects model was fitted to handle dependent effect sizes. Clinical relevance was assessed using posterior probabilities of exceeding the minimal clinically important difference (MCID, defined as g ≤ -0.39). Moderators were examined through subgroup analyses and meta-regressions.
RESULTS: Twenty-one RCTs (1,707 participants, 66 effect sizes) were included. Walking produced a medium-to-large improvement in subjective sleep quality (g = -0.76, 95% credible interval: -0.99 to -0.55), with extreme Bayesian evidence (Bayes factor > 10) and a 99.97% posterior probability of exceeding the MCID. The 95% prediction interval fell entirely below zero. Baseline Pittsburgh Sleep Quality Index score was the strongest moderator ( = -0.302), with worse baseline sleep associated with larger effects. Supervision mode and exercise setting did not meaningfully influence outcomes. GRADE certainty of evidence was very low.
CONCLUSION: Current evidence suggests that walking may improve subjective sleep quality in adults, with a 99.97% posterior probability of reaching the prespecified minimal clinically important difference, although evidence certainty is very low. Moderate-intensity walking three to five times weekly, 30 to 60 min per session, for 12 to 24 weeks may serve as a feasible prescription window, particularly for those with poorer baseline sleep. Future RCTs incorporating objective sleep measures are needed.
SYSTEMATIC REVIEW REGISTRATION: PROSPERO, CRD420261351897.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Core-7. Does Resistance Training Improve the Quality of Life of People With Parkinson's Disease? Evidence and Recommendations for Clinical Application Through a Systematic Review and Meta-Analysis of Randomized Clinical Trials.

- Candidate bucket: Core
- 事前スコア: 15
- PMID: 42370476
- DOI: 10.1002/pri.70266
- Journal: Physiotherapy research international : the journal for researchers and clinicians in physical therapy
- PubDate: 2026-07-01
- PublicationType: Journal Article; Systematic Review; Meta-Analysis; Review
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42370476/
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
BACKGROUND: Parkinson's disease is a neurological condition with motor and non-motor symptoms that negatively affect well-being and quality of life.
OBJECTIVE: This review aimed to analyze the effects of resistance training on quality of life in individuals with Parkinson's disease and to summarize recommendations for clinical application.
DATA SOURCES: Following PRISMA recommendations, searches were conducted in Web of Science, PubMed, EMBASE (with ClinicalTrials.gov), PEDro, CINAHL, and Scopus.
STUDY SELECTION: RCTs were included that compared the effects of resistance training with other therapeutic modalities or a control group on the quality of life in people with Parkinson's.
DATA EXTRACTION AND SYNTHESIS: Data were extracted using Microsoft Excel and analyzed in RevMan. The risk of bias was assessed using the RoB 2 tool, the protocol reporting completeness was evaluated using CERT and certainty of the evidence was rated using GRADE.
RESULTS: Fourteen studies were included, featuring highly heterogeneous protocols. Resistance training was superior to control (SMD -0.81; CI -1.45 to -0.18; I 88%; moderate certainty of the evidence), although no significant difference was found compared to other therapeutic modalities (SMD -0.02; CI -0.44 to 0.41; low certainty of the evidence). Exploratory subgroup analyses suggested a trend toward more favorable results in trials lasting longer than 12 weeks, involving patients with mild-to-moderate disease severity (H&Y ≤ 3), and reporting high protocol completeness (CERT > 11). Most of the studies were classified as having a low risk of bias and presented a moderate description of the protocols in the CERT.
LIMITATIONS: The included studies exhibited high heterogeneity and required data imputation for missing standard deviations. Additionally, exploratory subgroup analyses were underpowered due to the limited number of trials.
CONCLUSIONS: Current evidence suggests that resistance training may improve quality of life in individuals with Parkinson's disease. Exploratory subgroup analyses tentatively suggest potential trends favoring mild-to-moderate stages and intervention exceeding 12 weeks, while being a safe practice. However, high heterogeneity limits the certainty of the evidence. Future studies should prioritize standardized reporting (CERT) to ensure intervention reproducibility.
TRIAL REGISTRATION: PROSPERO re

## ダイエット・筋トレ Core-8. GERD remission and safety profile of Single Anastomosis Sleeve Ileal (SASI) bypass vs sleeve gastrectomy (SG): a systematic review and meta-analysis.

- Candidate bucket: Core
- 事前スコア: 15
- PMID: 42377474
- DOI: 10.1007/s00464-026-12737-1
- Journal: Surgical endoscopy
- PubDate: 2026-04
- PublicationType: Journal Article; Meta-Analysis; Systematic Review; Comparative Study
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42377474/
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
INTRODUCTION: Sleeve gastrectomy (SG) is widely recognized for its association with gastroesophageal reflux disease (GERD) and reduced sustained weight loss in the long term. The Single Anastomosis Sleeve Ileal (SASI) bypass was introduced as an alternative to enhance the metabolic benefits of SG, improve GERD outcomes, address nutritional challenges of ileal bypasses, and maintain duodenal access.
METHODS: This study is a systematic review and meta-analysis of the comparative safety and efficacy of SASI bypass vs SG. A literature search in PubMed, Scopus, Embase, and Cochrane identified 234 articles after duplicate removal. Primary outcomes were GERD remission and complication rates over the follow-up period of each study including all complications reported by the authors, while secondary outcomes included weight loss and obesity-related condition remission.
RESULTS: Thirteen studies, including 2 RCTs and eleven observational studies, analyzed 960 SG and 396 SASI bypass patients. SASI bypass showed significantly higher GERD remission (OR 7.64; 95% CI [2.81; 20.78]; P < 0.001; I = 0%) but with an overall higher complication rate after sensitivity analysis (OR 4.39; 95% CI [1.44-13.40]; P = 0.009; I = 59%). It also had superior excess weight loss (MD = 9.61; 95% CI [5.8; 13.43]; P < 0.01) and better dyslipidemia remission (OR 2.19; 95% CI [1.07; 4.48]; P = 0.031). Hypertension and OSA remission rates were similar between techniques. Type 2 diabetes mellitus (T2D) remission rates were high after SASI bypass (OR 4.20; 95% CI [2.17; 8.11]; P < 0.001).
CONCLUSION: SASI bypass offers superior GERD remission over SG but with potentially higher associated morbidity. Both techniques effectively promote weight loss and obesity-related condition remission, with SASI having a slight metabolic advantage due to intestinal bypass. Further research including prospective studies are needed to validate these findings and optimize postoperative care.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Core-9. Effects of exercise interventions on core health outcomes in patients with SLE: systematic review and meta-analysis.

- Candidate bucket: Core
- 事前スコア: 15
- PMID: 42373138
- DOI: 10.1136/lupus-2026-002027
- Journal: Lupus science & medicine

Abstract:
OBJECTIVES: This meta-analysis evaluated the effects of exercise interventions on key health outcomes in adults with SLE, including fatigue, physical function, aerobic capacity, disease activity, depression and pain.
METHODS: Following the Preferred Reporting Items for Systematic Reviews and Meta-Analyses (PRISMA) 2020 guidelines, we systematically searched four databases up to February 2025 for randomised controlled trials (RCTs) in adults diagnosed with SLE according to the American College of Rheumatology/European Alliance of Associations for Rheumatology (ACR/EULAR) criteria. Eligible studies examined aerobic, resistance or combined exercise as the sole intervention. Meta-analyses were conducted using Hedges' g, the Risk of Bias 2 (ROB-2) tool and the Grading of Recommendations Assessment, Development and Evaluation (GRADE) system used to assess bias and evidence quality.
RESULTS: Twelve RCTs involving 470 participants were included. Exercise showed small-to-moderate improvements in fatigue (g=-0.53, 95% CI -0.81 to -0.25, p<0.001), physical function (g=0.46, 95% CI 0.23 to 0.68, p<0.001), aerobic capacity (g=0.47, 95% CI 0.22 to 0.71, p<0.001), depression (g=-0.36, 95% CI -0.64 to -0.09, p=0.01) and pain (g=-0.53, 95% CI -0.86 to -0.20, p<0.001), with no significant change in disease activity (g=0.18, 95% CI -0.16 to 0.51, p=0.30). GRADE rated the evidence as moderate for fatigue, physical function, depression and pain, and low for other outcomes.
CONCLUSION: Exercise is an effective non-pharmacological therapy in SLE management, improving several physical and psychological outcomes. Individualised, moderate-intensity and supervised programmes are recommended. Further research should optimise intervention protocols and evaluate long-term safety.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Core-10. Compliance With Physical Activity, Sedentary Behaviour and Sleep Recommendations in Children Aged 5-13 Years: A Systematic Review and Meta-Analysis Across 15 Countries.

Abstract:
BACKGROUND: Several regions have published 24-h Movement Guidelines recommending durations of moderate-to-vigorous physical activity (MVPA), recreational screen time (ST) and sleep. This study aimed to investigate the global prevalence of school-aged children meeting the individual and combined recommendations of the 24-h Movement Guidelines.
METHOD: Six databases were initially searched from 2016 to 2025 and further updated in May 2026. This review included studies reporting adherence rates to the 24-h Movement Guidelines, including none, individual (MVPA, ST, sleep), combined (MVPA&ST, MVPA&sleep, ST&sleep) and all three guidelines among children aged 5-13 years. ## ダイエット・筋トレ Reserve-2. Investigating the Effect of Blood Groups on the Risk of Musculoskeletal Injuries: A Systematic Review.

Previous studies have examined the relationship between blood groups and metabolic diseases. However, no study has yet investigated the relationship between blood groups and musculoskeletal injuries, and this issue has not been fully clarified. This systematic review investigates the association between blood groups and the risk of musculoskeletal injuries.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Reserve-3. Efficacy of different exercise modalities for sleep quality in Parkinson's disease: a systematic review and network meta-analysis.

Abstract:
BACKGROUND: Sleep disturbances are a common and burdensome non-motor symptom in Parkinson's disease (PD). The comparative efficacy of different exercise modalities for sleep quality in PD remains unclear. This network meta-analysis (NMA) aimed to compare and rank the effects of various exercise interventions on sleep quality in people with PD.
METHODS: This study followed the PRISMA extension statement for network meta-analyses. A systematic search was performed across Web of Science, Embase, PubMed, the Cochrane Library, Scopus, CNKI, and Wanfang databases from their inception to November 3, 2025. Eligible randomized controlled trials (RCTs) were identified, with study selection, data extraction, and bias assessment conducted independently by two reviewers. NMA was performed using Stata 19.0. Consistency was examined using design-by-treatment interaction and node-splitting approaches. Rankings were estimated using the surface under the cumulative ranking curve (SUCRA).
RESULTS: Of 2309 records screened, 16 RCTs involving 932 people with PD were included. Aerobic exercise (AE) significantly improved sleep quality compared with control (SMD = -0.94, 95% CI: -1.82 to -0.07). SUCRA rankings were: AE (highest) > multimodal exercise (MME) > resistance training (RT) > stretching training (ST) > mind-body exercise (MBE) > control. No significant publication bias was found (Egger's test, P = 0.438).
CONCLUSION: This NMA indicates that aerobic exercise is the most promising modality for enhancing sleep quality in people with PD and may guide non-pharmacological treatment selection in clinical practice.
SYSTEMATIC REVIEW REGISTRATION: https://www.crd.york.ac.uk/prospero/, identifier CRD420261341953.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Reserve-5. Efficacy of prophylactic ursodeoxycholic acid in preventing gallstone formation after metabolic bariatric surgery: an updated systematic review and meta-analysis of randomized controlled trials.

- Candidate bucket: Reserve
- 事前スコア: 9
- PMID: 42380928
- DOI: 10.1186/s12893-026-03983-0
- Journal: BMC surgery
- PubDate: 2026-06-30
- PublicationType: Journal Article; Systematic Review
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42380928/
- OA URL: https://doi.org/10.1186/s12893-026-03983-0
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
BACKGROUND: Rapid weight loss following Metabolic bariatric surgery (MBS) is associated with an increased risk of developing de novo gallstone formation. We aimed to evaluate the efficacy of prophylactic ursodeoxycholic acid (UDCA) in preventing gallstone formation and reducing gallstone-related outcomes after MBS.
METHODS: We conducted a systematic review and meta-analysis of randomized controlled trials (RCTs) following the PRISMA guidelines through PubMed/MEDLINE, Cochrane, Embase, Scopus, Google Scholar, and clinicaltrials.gov. The primary outcome was gallstone formation at 12-24 months, while symptomatic gallstones and cholecystectomy incidence were secondary outcomes. Pooled risk ratios (RRs) with 95% confidence intervals (CIs) were calculated using random-effects models. Subgroup analysis was conducted according to UDCA dose, duration of administration, and the type of operation. Meta-regression was performed to assess the effect of age and baseline BMI on gallstone formation. I and Cochrane Q p-value were used to assess the heterogeneity of the studies.
RESULTS: Ten RCTs, including 3,575 participants, were included. Prophylactic UDCA reduced the incidence of gallstone formation by 67% at 12-24 months, and 73% at 6 months, while symptomatic gallstones were reduced by 70%. No statistically significant difference was found in the cholecystectomy rates. Subgroup analysis showed that UDCA doses of 500-600 mg daily administered for 6-12 months were effective, with no significant differences in gallstone formation between surgical procedures. Meta-regression analysis showed a slight increase in gallstone risk with age and a slight decrease with higher BMI, although neither relationship reached statistical significance.
CONCLUSIONS: Prophylactic UDCA may be an effective preventive measure for gallstone formation in MBS patients, however additional studies are needed to assess its effect on cholecystectomy.
TRIAL REGISTRATION: The systematic review was registered in PROSPERO under registration number CRD420251004594.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Reserve-6. Effect of home-based cardiac rehabilitation on quality of life, health behaviours and cardiac anxiety in patients with coronary artery disease: findings from a single-blinded randomised controlled trial.

- Candidate bucket: Reserve
- 事前スコア: 9
- PMID: 42379722
- DOI: 10.1136/bmjopen-2025-114349
- Journal: BMJ open
- PubDate: 2026-06-30
- PublicationType: Journal Article; Randomized Controlled Trial
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42379722/
- OA URL: https://doi.org/10.1136/bmjopen-2025-114349
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
OBJECTIVE: To evaluate the effectiveness of a contextually developed home-based cardiac rehabilitation (HBCR) programme on heart-related quality of life (QoL), cardiac health behaviours (CHB) and cardiac anxiety (CA) among patients with coronary artery disease (CAD) in Lahore, Pakistan.
DESIGN: Single-blinded randomised controlled trial (RCT).
SETTING: Cardiology department of a public tertiary-care hospital in Lahore, Pakistan.
PARTICIPANTS: 120 patients aged 18-65 years diagnosed with coronary artery disease who had undergone percutaneous coronary intervention or medical management were recruited and randomly allocated to intervention (n=60) and control (n=60) groups.
INTERVENTION: Participants in the intervention group received a nurse-led HBCR programme consisting of discharge education, structured physical activity and exercise guidance, dietary counselling, medication adherence support, and regular telephonic and physical follow-ups over 24 weeks. The control group received routine care and standard discharge advice.
PRIMARY OUTCOME MEASURES: Primary outcomes were heart-related quality of life (MacNew HRQoL), cardiac health behaviours (Cardiac Health Behaviour Scale-21) and cardiac anxiety (Cardiac Anxiety Questionnaire-18), assessed at baseline, 3 months and 6 months postdischarge.
RESULTS: At 6-month follow-up, the intervention group demonstrated significantly higher global QoL scores compared with the control group (mean difference 30.71, 95% CI 22.90 to 38.50). CHB scores were also significantly higher in the intervention group (mean difference 19.60, 95% CI 16.20 to 23.00). CA scores were significantly lower among participants receiving HBCR (mean difference -18.72, 95% CI -21.00 to -16.40). These improvements were evident after 3 months and sustained at 6 months.
CONCLUSION: The nurse-led HBCR programme significantly improved QoL and CHB and reduced CA among patients with CAD. HBCR may provide an effective and scalable secondary prevention strategy in settings where centre-based cardiac rehabilitation services are limited.
TRIAL REGISTRATION: Australian New Zealand Clinical Trial Registry, ACTRN12623000049673p.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Reserve-7. Effects of maximal versus submaximal intended velocity resistance training on muscular fitness adaptations in older adults: A systematic review and meta-analysis.

- Journal: Sports medicine and health science

- OA URL: https://doi.org/10.1016/j.smhs.2026.03.001
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
PURPOSE: This systematic review aimed to: 1) explore muscular fitness adaptations (e.g., muscle mass, muscle strength, functional performance) in older adults (≥ 60 years) following exercise with resistance training compared to control; and 2) investigate the moderating effects of load intensity, training frequency, and movement velocity on muscular fitness adaptations.
METHODS: Four databases were searched (April 2024, updated 2025). Pooled effects for each outcome were summarized using Standardized Mean Difference (Hedges' ) through a three-level meta-analysis model, and subgroup was used to explore moderators. The certainty of evidence was assessed using the GRADE approach.
RESULTS: Sixteen studies were eligible ( = 801), with data available from fifteen moderate quality randomized controlled trials. Compared to control, resistance training was effective in improving muscle mass ( 0.16, = 67%), muscle strength ( 0.55, = 11%), and functional performance ( 0.76, = 62%). MaxV ( 0.93) resistance training with moderate intensity ( 0.71) and low frequency ( 0.64) was superior for improving functional performance.
CONCLUSIONS: Resistance training effectively enhances muscular fitness in older adults. Load intensity, frequency, and movement velocity (SubmaxV was better for muscle mass and muscle strength compared to MaxV, and MaxV for functional performance) may significantly modulate improvements in muscular fitness adaptations.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Reserve-9. Nutrition interventions in women with polycystic ovary syndrome: a systematic review.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Reserve-10. Effects of beta-alanine supplementation on exercise performance and related physiological outcomes in women: a systematic review and meta-analysis.

- Candidate bucket: Reserve
- 事前スコア: 9
- PMID: 42370349
- DOI: 10.3389/fnut.2026.1857513
- Journal: Frontiers in nutrition
- PubDate: 2026
- PublicationType: Journal Article; Systematic Review
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42370349/
- OA URL: https://www.frontiersin.org/journals/nutrition/articles/10.3389/fnut.2026.1857513/pdf
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
BACKGROUND: Beta-alanine is widely used as an ergogenic aid in sports nutrition, yet most evidence comes from male or mixed-sex samples. Its effects in women therefore remain unclear. This systematic review and meta-analysis examined the effects of beta-alanine supplementation on exercise performance and related outcomes in women.
METHODS: This review followed PRISMA 2020 guidelines and was registered in PROSPERO (CRD420261362733). PubMed, Web of Science, Scopus, the Cochrane Library, and Embase were searched from inception to April 30, 2026. Randomized controlled studies in women comparing beta-alanine with placebo or control were included. Outcomes included time to exhaustion (TTE), maximal or peak oxygen uptake, peak power, anaerobic performance, and body fat percentage. RoB 2 and GRADE were used to assess risk of bias and certainty of evidence, respectively. Random-effects meta-analyses were conducted using standardized mean differences with 95% confidence intervals.
RESULTS: Twelve reports from 11 independent randomized controlled trials involving 312 women were included. Beta-alanine supplementation showed a pooled effect in favor of TTE (8 studies, = 187; SMD = 0.49, 95% CI 0.20 to 0.79; = 0.001; I = 0%). For the remaining outcomes, pooled estimates were imprecise, with 95% confidence intervals including trivial and, where applicable, potentially meaningful effects. Moreover, certainty of evidence was very low for all outcomes after downgrading for risk of bias, imprecision, and publication bias; peak power and anaerobic performance were additionally downgraded for indirectness.
CONCLUSION: Beta-alanine supplementation may improve TTE in trials conducted in women, but current evidence does not support clear pooled effects on peak power, anaerobic performance, VO₂max and VO₂peak, or body fat percentage. Overall, these findings suggest an outcome-specific response pattern, although confidence in the evidence remains limited because of the small evidence base and very low certainty across outcomes.
SYSTEMATIC REVIEW REGISTRATION: https://www.crd.york.ac.uk/PROSPERO/view/CRD420261362733, identifier PROSPERO (CRD420261362733).

## ダイエット・筋トレ Reserve-13. Efficacy of botulinum toxin for masseter muscle hypertrophy: A systematic review and meta-analysis.

- PublicationType: Journal Article; Review
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42379083/
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
BACKGROUND: Masseter muscle hypertrophy (MMH) is a benign condition that can alter lower facial contour and cause esthetic concern. Botulinum toxin type A (BoNTA) is widely used as a minimally invasive treatment; however, the magnitude and consistency of its benefit remain uncertain.
METHODS: We performed a systematic review and meta-analysis of randomized, placebo-controlled trials evaluating BoNTA for MMH treatment. The Cochrane CENTRAL, Embase, and PubMed databases were searched. The primary outcome was change in masseter muscle thickness (MMT) during maximal clenching. CONCLUSIONS: BoNTA appears to provide short-term improvement in masseter prominence, muscle thickness, and patient-reported outcomes in MMH compared with placebo. Nominal 48 U and 72 U regimens were associated with benefit, but current evidence is insufficient to define a formulation-adjusted dose-response relationship or an optimal treatment protocol. Further standardized randomized trials with longer follow-up are needed.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Reserve-15. Serum vitamin D levels in non-obese women with polycystic ovary syndrome: a systematic review and meta-analysis.

- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
INTRODUCTION: Vitamin D deficiency is linked to increased risk of polycystic ovary syndrome (PCOS) and may worsen metabolic disorders such as insulin resistance. However, evidence remains inconsistent regarding vitamin D status in non-obese women with PCOS. This study aimed to perform the first systematic review and meta-analysis evaluating serum vitamin D levels in non-obese PCOS patients.

Subgroup analyses indicated that CAF + CHO mouth rinsing (g = 0.91, CI: 0.49-1.33) yielded superior effects compared to CAF + CHO ingestion (g = 0.33, CI: 0.14-0.52) ( for subgroup < 0.05). Performance improvements with CAF + CHO were observed for CHO- and placebo-controlled trials, but not in CAF-controlled trials, without significant subgroup effects ( for subgroup > 0.05). Importantly, evidence of publication bias was identified, and the overall certainty of evidence was graded as low according to the GRADE framework. : CAF + CHO appears to be effective for enhancing HIIE performance, with greater benefits observed when CHO is administered via mouth rinsing rather than ingestion. Preliminary evidence suggests that CAF may play a key role in CAF + CHO strategies. However, given the limited number of female participants, the generalizability of these findings to both sexes is limited. Additional high-quality trials are needed to establish more definitive recommendations.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Reserve-17. Hyperbaric Oxygen Treatment for Enhancing Athletic Recovery: A Systematic Review and Meta-Analysis.

- Candidate bucket: Reserve
- 事前スコア: 8
- PMID: 42365952
- DOI: 
- Journal: Undersea & hyperbaric medicine : journal of the Undersea and Hyperbaric Medical Society, Inc
- PubDate: 2026
- PublicationType: Journal Article; Systematic Review; Meta-Analysis
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42365952/
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
INTRODUCTION: Hyperbaric oxygen treatment (HBO₂) uses increased atmospheric pressure and fractional oxygen to enhance tissue oxygen delivery. HBO₂ has gained attention as a tool for athletic recovery and performance, but past reviews in the literature are limited or inconclusive. This systematic review and meta-analysis aim to provide an update and assess the effect of HBO₂ on athletic recovery.
METHODS: Literature searches were performed across PubMed, Cochrane Central, Google Scholar, and Embase (January 1, 2015-September 15, 2024), following PRISMA guidelines. Studies included healthy athletes undergoing HBO₂ to assess athletic performance, metabolic recovery, and physiological responses. Quality assessment was performed using Cochrane's risk of bias tools (ROB2 and ROBINS-1). A meta-analysis with subgroup analyses by age, body mass index, and body fat mass percentage was conducted, along with a meta-regression examining HBO₂ protocol characteristics and outcomes.
RESULTS: Eleven met the eligibility criteria; six studies were included in the meta-analysis. The meta-analysis showed that HBO₂ significantly reduced post-recovery blood lactate levels (effect size: -1.71; 95% CI: -3.10 to -0.32). Subgroup analysis revealed that younger athletes and those with lower fat mass receiving HBO₂ exhibited significant reductions in post-recovery lactate levels. Meta-regression was inconclusive but suggested treatment effect heterogeneity based on HBO₂ protocol characteristics. HBO₂ showed limited application in short-term power output and force production.
DISCUSSION: Hyperbaric oxygen treatment is an efficient method for improving athletic performance, particularly by reducing post-exercise lactate levels, thereby supporting faster metabolic recovery. Future studies should focus on standardized protocols, diverse populations, and long-term outcomes to better understand HBO₂'s potential in orthopedics and sports medicine.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Reserve-18. Effect of glucagon-like peptide-1 receptor agonists on major adverse cardiovascular events in adults with type 2 diabetes and established atherosclerotic cardiovascular disease: systematic review and meta-analysis of randomised trials.

- Candidate bucket: Reserve
- 事前スコア: 8
- PMID: 42376130
- DOI: 10.1097/XCE.0000000000000360
- Journal: Cardiovascular endocrinology & metabolism
- PubDate: 2026-09-01
- PublicationType: Journal Article; Review
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42376130/
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
Cardiovascular outcome trials suggest that glucagon-like peptide-1 receptor agonists (GLP-1RAs) reduce major adverse cardiovascular events in individuals with type 2 diabetes (T2DM), but the magnitude of benefit, including recent evidence from the landmark SOUL trial and oral formulations, remains uncertain. We performed a Preferred Reporting Items for Systematic Reviews and Meta-Analyses 2020 (International Prospective Register of Systematic Reviews ID: CRD420251034652), searching PubMed, Embase, Cochrane CENTRAL, Scopus and ClinicalTrials.gov on 6 May 2025 for randomised controlled trials comparing GLP-1RAs with placebo or usual care in adults with T2DM and established atherosclerotic cardiovascular disease. Seven trials, including 56 191 participants (mean follow-up: 3.5 years), were analysed. GLP-1RAs reduced major adverse cardiovascular events by 11% [hazard ratio: 0.89, 95% confidence interval (CI): 0.83-0.96], all-cause mortality by 11% (hazard ratio: 0.89, 95% CI: 0.82-0.97) and hospitalisation for heart failure by 7% (hazard ratio: 0.93, 95% CI: 0.89-0.98), all with high-certainty evidence. Overall, GLP-1RAs - available in subcutaneous and oral formulations - provide clinically meaningful cardiovascular benefits in high-risk adults with T2DM.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Reserve-19. Metabolic obesity phenotypic stability, dynamic transformation and risk of hypertension: a 10-year prospective cohort study in southwest China.

- Candidate bucket: Reserve
- 事前スコア: 8
- PMID: 42374120
- DOI: 10.1038/s41366-026-02140-0
- Journal: International journal of obesity (2005)
- PubDate: 2026-06-29
- PublicationType: Journal Article
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42374120/
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
INTRODUCTION: Hypertension is a major public health concern. Although metabolic obesity phenotypes are key risk factors for cardiovascular disease, the association between their dynamic changes and hypertension incidence remains unclear.
METHODS: Based on the Guizhou Population Health Cohort Study (GPHCS), after excluding participants with hypertension at baseline or incomplete data, a total of 3399 subjects were included in the final analysis. Participants were classified into four phenotypes based on body mass index (BMI) and metabolic status: metabolically healthy normal weight (MHNW), metabolically unhealthy normal weight (MUNW), metabolically healthy obesity (MHO), and metabolically unhealthy obesity (MUO). Cox proportional hazards models were applied to assess the associations between 16 phenotype transition patterns and the risk of hypertension, with robustness confirmed through multiple sensitivity analyses.
RESULTS: Over a median follow-up of 6.42 years, 826 incident cases of hypertension were identified. After multivariable adjustment, compared with MHNW, baseline MHO (HR = 1.26, 95% CI: 1.02-1.55) and MUO (HR = 1.50, 95% CI: 1.22-1.82) were positively associated with hypertension risk, whereas MUNW was not (HR = 1.10, 95% CI: 0.91-1.33). Dynamic analysis showed that 48.75% of participants underwent phenotypic transitions during follow-up. The two most prominent changes were that 37.38% of individuals with MUNW transitioned to MHNW and 31.21% of those with MHO transitioned to MUO. Transitions from any baseline phenotype to MHNW were not associated with a statistically significant increase in hypertension risk (all P > 0.05). All other phenotypic transitions were positively associated. Even participants who remained MHO experienced increased hypertension risk (HR = 2.30, 95% CI: 1.45-3.64).
CONCLUSION: Within the study population, MHO is an unstable state athat tended to progress to MUO, which carries the highest risk of hypertension. In contrast, the MUNW phenotype exhibits high reversibility and can revert to the MHNW phenotype. Future our studies require confirm whether early lifestyle interventions targeting metabolic health can effectively reduce the risk of hypertension.

## ダイエット・筋トレ Reserve-20. Effects of Modest Carbohydrate-Energy Supplementation on Resistance Training Adaptations in Trained Men: A Crossover Trial.

- Candidate bucket: Reserve
- 事前スコア: 7
- PMID: 42356347
- DOI: 10.3390/nu18121961
- Journal: Nutrients
- PubDate: 2026-06-17
- PublicationType: Journal Article; Randomized Controlled Trial
- PubMed: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42356347/
- OA URL: https://www.mdpi.com/2072-6643/18/12/1961/pdf?version=1781708904
- OpenAlex cited_by_count: 0

Abstract:
Higher energy and carbohydrate intakes have been hypothesized to enhance resistance training adaptations, yet empirical evidence remains mixed. The purpose of this study was to investigate whether supplemental carbohydrate-energy intake improves muscle hypertrophy and strength. Twenty resistance-trained men (26.7 ± 4.9 years old, 9.7 ± 6.1 years training experience) completed a quasi-randomized, double-blinded, counterbalanced crossover trial. Participants consumed either a daily protein-only supplement (30 g protein, 4 g carbohydrate) or a daily protein-plus-carbohydrate supplement (30 g protein, 54 g carbohydrate) for 8 weeks each, followed by crossover, while continuing their habitual training and nutrition. Primary outcomes included lean mass obtained using dual-energy X-ray absorptiometry, muscle thickness and cross-sectional area obtained via ultrasound, back squat one-repetition maximum, fatigue index, and knee extensor peak torque. Differences in estimated marginal means, controlling for order and phase effects, were analyzed via linear mixed models, with first-phase-only ANCOVAs as sensitivity analyses. The carbohydrate-protein condition resulted in significantly higher daily energy (+485 kcal/d; = 0.017) and carbohydrate intake (+33 g/d; = 0.043) than the protein-only condition, with no differences in protein or fat intake or training volume. No significant differences between conditions were observed for any outcome, including in the sensitivity analyses. Modest supplemental carbohydrate-energy intake did not significantly augment muscle hypertrophy, fatigue resistance or strength in trained men within our study context. More high-powered research is needed to determine how much and under which circumstances carbohydrate-energy intake affects resistance training adaptations.

### Interesting-1. Efficacy of Metformin in Prevention of Glucocorticoid-Induced Hyperglycemia in Patients Without Diabetes: A Meta-Analysis.
- Genre: 抗老化
- Interesting topic score: 15
- Quality score: 13
- PMID: 42332417
- DOI: 10.1002/edm2.70235
- Journal: Endocrinology, diabetes & metabolism
- Pub date: 2026-07-01
- Publication types: Journal Article; Meta-Analysis; Review
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42332417/
- Abstract: PURPOSE: The glucocorticoids are increasingly being used in the management of different autoimmune conditions and cancers. Our meta-analysis aims to leverage metformin's potential to reverse the metabolic complications of glucocorticoids by activating AMP-activated protein kinase (AMPK), while sparing their anti-inflammatory benefits.
METHODS: PubMed, Cochrane Library, trial registries and Google Scholar were searched from inception to June 2025 for Randomized Controlled Trials (RCTs) and observational studies comparing metformin and placebo to prevent metabolic side effects of glucocorticoid therapy in non-diabetic patients. After screening by two independent reviewers according to PRISMA guidelines, four studies involving 187 patients were analysed using the random-effects model in RevMan 5.4.1, and mean differences (MD) were calculated.
RESULTS: Preventive metformin administration during glucocorticoid treatment is superior to placebo with respect to glycaemic control as shown by statistically significant reduction in fasting blood glucose [MD = -0.60 (95% CI: -0.86 to -0.34)], HOMA index of insulin resistance [MD = -0.53 (95% CI: -0.97 to -0.08)], LDL levels [MD = -0.20 (95% CI: -0.40 to -0.00)] and total cholesterol [MD = -0.27 (95% CI: -0.54 to -0.01)]. However, our study failed to show significant improvement in area under the curve glucose (mmol/L × min) after challenge [MD = -176.66 (95% CI: -415.42, 62.11)], basal metabolic rate (BMR) [MD = 51.99 (95% CI: -53.08, 157.07)], HDL [MD = -0.04 (95% CI: -0.13, 0.05)], insulin levels [MD = -2.26 (95% CI: -5.90, 1.38)], triglycerides [MD = -0.15 (95% CI: -0.42, 0.13)] and body weight [MD = -0.93 (95% CI: -2.29 to 0.44)].
CONCLUSION: While glucocorticoids remain essential in various clinical contexts, their detrimental effects on glucose metabolism are well documented. This study supports metformin as a promising preventive treatment in non-diabetic patients receiving systemic glucocorticoid therapy. Improvement in insulin sensitivity and resulting fasting glucose levels may offset glucocorticoid-exacerbated inflammation. Further studies are needed to address long-term outcomes, including adiposity, bone metabolism, appetite, liver function and muscle wasting, as well as to identify possible predictors of therapeutic response.
TRIAL REGISTRATION: International Prospective Register of Systematic Reviews (PRO

### Interesting-2. GLP-1 receptor agonists in pediatric obesity and diabetes: a systematic review of efficacy, metabolic effects, and safety.
- Genre: 抗老化
- Interesting topic score: 14
- Quality score: 8
- PMID: 42365860
- DOI: 10.1016/j.diabres.2026.113400
- Journal: Diabetes research and clinical practice
- Pub date: 2026-06-28
- Publication types: Journal Article; Review
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42365860/
- Abstract: Childhood obesity and youth-onset type 2 diabetes mellitus (T2DM) are increasing, highlighting the need for effective treatments beyond lifestyle intervention and metformin. This review systematically evaluated the efficacy and safety of glucagon-like peptide-1 receptor agonists (GLP-1 RAs) in children and adolescents with obesity or T2DM. PubMed-indexed studies published from 2000 to 2025 were reviewed, including seven pivotal randomized controlled trials and six meta-analyses involving 901 participants aged 6 to < 18 years. Semaglutide 2.4 mg/week produced the greatest BMI reduction in adolescents with obesity, followed by liraglutide 3.0 mg/day, which also improved BMI SDS in adolescents and younger children. In youth-onset T2DM, liraglutide 1.8 mg/day and dulaglutide significantly improved HbA1c compared with placebo. Weight-reducing agents also improved insulin resistance and modestly reduced triglycerides, while LDL-cholesterol changes were minimal. Gastrointestinal adverse events, mainly nausea and vomiting, were the most frequent and were generally transient and dose dependent. No significant adverse effects on linear growth or pubertal progression were reported. GLP-1 RAs are effective adjuncts for pediatric obesity and T2DM, but longer-term studies are needed to assess cardiovascular safety, bone health, and growth outcomes.

### Interesting-3. Effectiveness of Whole-Body Vibration Therapy on Handgrip Strength: A Systematic Review and Meta-Analysis of Randomized Controlled Trials.
- Genre: ダイエット・筋トレ
- Interesting topic score: 13
- Quality score: 20
- PMID: 42373946
- DOI: 10.1002/msc.70246
- Journal: Musculoskeletal care
- Pub date: 2026-09-01
- Publication types: Journal Article; Systematic Review; Meta-Analysis; Review; Research Support, Non-U.S. Gov't
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42373946/
- Abstract: INTRODUCTION: Although whole-body vibration (WBV) therapy has already demonstrated efficacy in improving lower-limb muscle strength, it is still unclear whether it has similar potential for improving handgrip strength.
OBJECTIVE: To verify the efficacy of WBV on handgrip strength.
METHODS: The search was conducted on September 5, 2025, in PubMed, Embase, CENTRAL, CINAHL, SPORTDiscus, Web of Science, LILACS, PEDro, and SciELO. Risk of bias was assessed via the PEDro scale, and certainty of evidence using GRADE. Meta-analyses were performed using the standardized mean difference (SMD) under random- or fixed-effects models according to heterogeneity levels.
RESULTS: Thirty-four studies (1272 participants) were included (32.4% had a high risk of bias). Compared with controls, acute WBV showed no significant effect on handgrip strength, with moderate-certainty evidence (SMD = 0.09, p = 0.34). Chronic WBV produced a significant but small effect, supported by very low-certainty evidence (SMD = 0.33, p = 0.01). Sensitivity analysis excluding high-risk-of-bias studies rendered the chronic effect non-significant (p = 0.07). Exploratory subgroup analyses of chronic interventions showed a significant interaction for body positioning (p = 0.02), with significant effects for direct hand contact (SMD = 0.76, p = 0.03) and static standing (SMD = 0.52, p = 0.03). Compared with resistance training, evidence was inconclusive and of very low certainty (SMD = -2.43, p = 0.25).
CONCLUSION: Chronic WBV involving direct hand contact may be associated with more pronounced effects on handgrip strength; however, these findings are exploratory, supported by very low-certainty evidence, and require confirmation by future trials.

- Pub year: 2026

- Intervention: 多面的生活習慣介入(運動・食事・認知トレーニング・血管リスク管理等)

- Importance reason: MASHは世界的に増加する肝疾患で、SGLT2阻害薬を含む複数の新薬が承認・申請段階にある。このNMAは治療選択の実践的根拠を提供する。
- Clinical relevance: MASH治療薬の選択優先度・組み合わせ戦略を判断する際の参考エビデンスとなる。内科・消化器・糖尿病科で直接活用可能。
- Novelty: SGLT2阻害薬を明示的にNMAネットワークに組み込んだ点が新規。
- Evidence strength: moderate
- Safety notes: 各薬剤の安全性プロファイルをNMAで比較。消化器副作用・心血管リスクの差異を確認する必要がある。
- Limitations: 間接比較のため結果の不確実性あり。試験デザイン・アウトカム定義の異質性が影響する可能性。
- Practice change potential: MASH治療の処方最適化に直接影響する可能性が高い
- Next action: 全文でSGLT2阻害薬を含む組み合わせ療法の詳細ランキング・確実性評価・サブグループ別効果量を確認する
- Watch keywords: MASH pharmacotherapy, SGLT2 inhibitors, network meta-analysis, GLP-1RA, FGF21, THR-beta, combination therapy, steatohepatitis
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42325618/
- OA URL: https://www.frontiersin.org/journals/endocrinology/articles/10.3389/fendo.2026.1829315/pdf
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42325618/, https://doi.org/10.3389/fendo.2026.1829315
- Summary: MASH薬物療法のNMA。SGLT2阻害薬を含む最新治療薬をGLP-1RA・FGF21・THR-βと同一ネットワークで比較し、組み合わせ療法の有効性・安全性をランク付け。治療選択の実践的根拠を提供する包括的エビデンス統合研究。
- Trend summary: GLP-1RAに続きSGLT2阻害薬・FGF21・THR-β等のMASH承認/申請が相次いでおり、比較NMAの需要が高まっている。
- Future outlook: 頭対頭RCTが少ない中、NMAが治療指針の中核となる見込み。組み合わせ療法の安全性データ蓄積が次の課題。
- Deep dive: true
- Deep dive reason: MASH治療領域で最新薬物療法をNMAで統合した高インパクト研究。消化器・糖尿病診療での意思決定に影響する可能性があるため詳細確認推奨。

- Novelty: 構造MRI・細胞病理・神経化学を単一フレームワークで統合した点が新規。
- Evidence strength: moderate
- Safety notes: 基礎・疫学研究統合であり直接的な臨床安全性悇念はない。
- Limitations: 各研究の方法論・対象集団の異質性。因果関係の確立には縦断研究が必要。
- Practice change potential: VCI診断・層別化の改善に寄与する可能性があるが、直接的な診療変更には時間を要する
- Next action: 全文で主要な構造萎縮ネットワーク・神経化学マーカー・治療標的候補を確認する
- Watch keywords: vascular cognitive impairment, structural atrophy network, neurochemical substrate, cerebrovascular disease dementia, VCI biomarker
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42323464/
- OA URL: 
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42323464/
- Summary: 血管性認知障害の多スケールマッピング研究。構造萎縮ネットワーク・細胞・神経化学基盤を統合し、局所血管障害が全脳ネットワーク障害を引き起こすメカニズムを解明。VCI早期診断・治療標的探索への寄与が期待される。

- Rank: 10
- Score: 52
- Importance level: moderate
- PMID: 42324178

- Study design: Systematic review / Meta-analysis

- Limitations: 試験間のFFM測定法の異質性（DXA vs BIA等）。フォローアップ期間のばらつき。
- Practice change potential: GLP-1RA使用中の運動処方の標準化を促す可能性がある
- Next action: 全文でGLP-1RA vs GIP/GLP-1のFFM変化の差・運動追加による効果量・サルコペニア関連アウトカムを確認する
- Watch keywords: GLP-1RA lean mass, fat-free mass weight loss, incretin therapy body composition, bariatric surgery FFM, exercise GLP-1
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42324178/
- OA URL: 
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42324178/
- Summary: GLP-1RA・食事運動・肥満外科手術の除脂肖体重（FFM）への影響 SR/MA。GLP-1RA使用時のFFM損失と運動追加による軽減効果を定量化。体組成管理の観点からGLP-1RA治療中の運動処方追加を支持するエビデンス。
- Trend summary: GLP-1RAの普及とともに体重減少の「質」（筋肉量保持）が重要テーマに浮上。運動との組み合わせ最適化研究が急増している。

- Population: 肥満・2型糖尿病患者（RCT複数)

- Comparison: プラセボまたは対照群

- Practice change potential: GLP-1RA処方に筋肉喪失対策の運動指導を組み込む標準化を加速しうる。
- Next action: 全文でGLP-1RA種別・用量別の除脂肪体重変化量と異質性を確認。運動介入との比較サブグループがあれば抽出する。

- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42319968/
- OA URL: 
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42319968/, https://doi.org/10.1002/dmrr.70194
- Summary: RCT SR/MAでGLP-1RAが除脂肪体重を有意に減少させることを示した。SGLT2阻害薬の影響は相対的に小さい。急拡大する減量薬処方において筋肉喪失リスクを定量化し、運動介入併用の必要性を支持する。PCOS・妊娠前肥満管理にも直接波及する重要エビデンス。
- Trend summary: GLP-1RA使用拡大に伴い筋肉喪失・骨密度低下への懸念が高まっており、体組成への影響を定量化するSR/MAが相次いでいる。
- Future outlook: GLP-1RA＋抵抗性運動の最適併用プロトコルを検討する大規模RCTが必要。産婦人科集団での特化した検討も期待される。

- Deep dive reason: GLP-1RA処方が急拡大する中、筋肉喪失リスク定量化は産婦人科・肥満外来を含む多科横断的な実装判断に直結するため。

- DOI: 10.1055/a-2884-9010
- Journal: American journal of perinatology
- Pub year: 2026
- Study design: 大規模後向きコホート（Consortium on Safe Labor）
- Population: Consortium on Safe Laborデータベースの妊婦・新生児（大規模多施設）
- Intervention: 妊娠中体重増加（GWG）の評価（IOM基準との比較）
- Comparison: GWG区分別（適切・過剰・不足）および母体BMI区分別
- Main outcome: 新生児低酸素イベント・外傷イベント
- Key findings: GWGと新生児低酸素・外傷の関連を大規模コホートで評価。過体重・肥満母体でのGWG最適範囲がIOM基準と異なる可能性を示唆。方法論的課題（GWGの測定法）も検討。
- Importance reason: IOM基準のGWG推奨を大規模データで検証し、過体重・肥満妊婦の管理指針に直結。新生児低酸素・外傷という臨床的に重要なアウトカムを使用。
- Clinical relevance: 妊婦体重管理指導、特に過体重・肥満妊婦のGWG目標設定の見直しに関連。
- Novelty: 新生児低酸素・外傷というアウトカムにフォーカスし、GWGの方法論的課題も同時検討した点。
- Evidence strength: moderate
- Safety notes: 観察研究。因果関係は不明。GWG測定の方法論的バイアスあり。
- Limitations: 後向きコホート、GWG測定の方法論的問題、残存交絡、Consortiumデータの施設偏り。
- Practice change potential: 中（肥満妊婦のGWG指導基準の再検討を促す可能性）
- Next action: 全文でBMI区分別のGWGと新生児アウトカムの効果推定値、IOM基準との比較、交絡調整法を確認する。

- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42302825/
- OA URL: 
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42302825/
- Summary: Consortium on Safe Laborの大規模データで妊娠中体重増加と新生児低酸素・外傷の関連を評価。過体重・肥満妊婦でのGWG最適範囲がIOM基準と異なる可能性を示唆。GWG測定法の方法論的課題も検討。
- Trend summary: 過体重・肥満妊婦に対するGWG推奨の精緻化研究が活発化。IOM基準の妥当性を問い直す研究が増加。
- Future outlook: 前向きRCTによるGWG介入が肥満妊婦の新生児アウトカムを改善するかの検証が期待される。
- Deep dive: true
- Deep dive reason: 大規模コホートで妊婦体重管理の臨床指針に直結する知見。IOM基準の妥当性を問い直す可能性があり、全文でBMI別の効果推定値確認が必要。

## 28. Natural versus artificial cycle for endometrial preparation in ovulatory women undergoing frozen-thawed embryo transfer: a randomised controlled trial

- Date: 2026-06-22
- Genre: 生殖
- Rank: 2
- Score: 80
- Importance level: high
- PMID: 42315758
- DOI: 10.1093/humrep/deag095
- Journal: Human Reproduction
- Pub year: 2026
- Study design: Randomized Controlled Trial
- Population: 排卵周期を有するFET施行女性
- Intervention: 自然周期による子宮内膜準備
- Comparison: 人工周期（エストロゲン＋プロゲステロン）
- Main outcome: 胎児心拍確認を伴う臨床妊娠率（CPR）
- Key findings: 排卵女性のFETで自然周期と人工周期のCPRは同等（非劣性）。自然周期は薬剤負担軽減・生理的環境温存の点で支持される。
- Importance reason: 排卵女性のFETプロトコル選択について、最高レベルのエビデンスを提供するRCT。日常の生殖医療プロトコルを変えうる。
- Clinical relevance: 排卵機能のある患者への不要なホルモン投与を回避し、患者負担軽減と自然な内膜環境の確保に直結する。
- Novelty: 自然周期vs人工周期のRCTとしてHuman Reproduction掲載の最新エビデンス。
- Evidence strength: high
- Safety notes: 自然周期ではLHサージのタイミング管理が必要で、排卵検出の見落としリスクに注意。人工周期には血栓リスクのエストロゲン投与が含まれる。
- Limitations: 単施設または限定施設；排卵女性のみへの適用で無排卵・PCOS患者への外挿は不可。
- Practice change potential: 排卵女性のFETでは自然周期を第一選択として標準化するプロトコル変更の根拠となりうる。
- Next action: 全文でLHサージ検出プロトコル・補足的黄体サポート有無・OHSS既往例への対応を確認。施設プロトコルとの比較検討。
- Watch keywords: FET natural cycle RCT, frozen embryo transfer protocol, endometrial preparation ovulatory, artificial cycle HRT
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42315758/
- OA URL: 
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42315758/, https://doi.org/10.1093/humrep/deag095
- Summary: 排卵女性のFETで自然周期と人工周期の臨床妊娠率が同等であることを示したRCT。自然周期は薬剤負担軽減と生理的内膜環境の観点から支持される。排卵機能のある患者への不要なホルモン投与を回避できるプロトコル転換の根拠。
- Trend summary: FETの内膜準備法については自然周期を支持するエビデンスが蓄積しており、特に排卵女性での自然周期優先の流れが加速している。
- Future outlook: PCOS・無排卵患者を含む幅広い集団への適用可能性と、妊娠・周産期アウトカムの長期比較研究が必要。
- Deep dive: true
- Deep dive reason: 生殖医療の日常プロトコルを直接変えうるRCTで、Human Reproductionのエビデンスとして実装判断に最直結するため。

## 29. Rethinking parenteral nutrition as supportive therapy for neonatal sepsis

- Date: 2026-06-22
- Genre: 周産期
- Rank: 3
- Score: 48
- Importance level: moderate
- PMID: 42302786
- DOI: 10.1016/j.medj.2026.101182
- Journal: Med (New York, N.Y.)
- Pub year: 2026
- Study design: Perspective・レビュー
- Population: 新生児（特に早産児）の敗血症患者
- Intervention: 非経口栄養（PN）の組成・タイミング最適化（免疫代謝的視点）
- Comparison: 従来のグルコース高含有PNと免疫調整型PNの概念比較
- Main outcome: 炎症制御・臓器傷害・臨床アウトカム（概念的）
- Key findings: 新生児敗血症に対するPNのガイドラインが不在。高グルコースPNは過剰な解糖系依存免疫応答を誘導しうる。免疫代謝学的観点からPNが炎症・臓器傷害を修飾しうるという概念的転換を提唱。
- Importance reason: NICU管理でガイドラインが存在しない空白領域に問題提起。免疫代謝学的視点からの栄養戦略は今後の研究方向性を示す。
- Clinical relevance: 新生児敗血症のNICU管理、特に非経口栄養処方の見直し議論に関連。
- Novelty: 免疫代謝学的メカニズムを用いてPNの組成が新生児免疫応答を能動的に制御できると主張した点。
- Evidence strength: low
- Safety notes: Perspectiveであり一次臨床データなし。前臨床モデルへの依存が大きい。
- Limitations: 一次データなし、前臨床モデル依存、ヒト新生児への外挿は要注意、無作為化試験なし。
- Practice change potential: 低（概念提唱段階、今後の研究待ち）
- Next action: 引用されている前臨床モデルのデータとヒト観察研究の質を確認する。
- Watch keywords: neonatal sepsis parenteral nutrition, immunometabolism neonatal nutrition, glucose parenteral nutrition inflammation, preterm sepsis nutritional support
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42302786/
- OA URL: 
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42302786/
- Summary: 新生児敗血症（特に早産児）における非経口栄養のガイドライン不在を問題提起するPerspective。高グルコースPNが免疫応答を過剰刺激しうるという免疫代謝学的概念転換を提唱。ヒト一次データはなく前臨床モデル依存。
- Trend summary: 新生児集中治療における栄養の免疫調節作用への関心が高まっている。
- Future outlook: 新生児敗血症に対する免疫代謝最適化PNの臨床試験設計が期待される。
- Deep dive: 
- Deep dive reason: Perspectiveであり一次データなし。概念的な問題提起にとどまる。

## 30. Plasma proteomic signatures of cellular aging predict human disease

- Date: 2026-06-22
- Genre: 抗老化
- Rank: 3
- Score: 78
- Importance level: high
- PMID: 42297981
- DOI: 10.1038/s41591-026-04446-y
- Journal: Nature Medicine
- Pub year: 2026
- Study design: 大規模コホート研究（機械学習・プロテオミクス）
- Population: 60,542例（血漿プロテオーム測定）
- Intervention: 細胞型特異的老化シグネチャーの血漿プロテオーム推定
- Comparison: 暦年齢・従来の老化バイオマーカー
- Main outcome: 細胞型別老化スコアによる疾患予測精度
- Key findings: 7,000超の血漿タンパク質から機械学習モデルで細胞型別老化スコアを構築。スコアは将来の疾患発症を予測し、老化が臓器・細胞種によって非同期であることを大規模に実証。
- Importance reason: 60,542例という超大規模サンプルでの血液ベース老化バイオマーカー確立はNature Medicine水準の突破口。非侵襲的な老化評価と疾患予測の新規アプローチを提示。
- Clinical relevance: 血液検査のみで個人の細胞型別老化プロファイルを評価し、疾患リスク層別化や抗老化介入の効果モニタリングへの応用が期待される。
- Novelty: 細胞型特異的老化を血漿プロテオームで推定した点。7,000超タンパク質・60,542例は前例のない規模。
- Evidence strength: moderate
- Safety notes: 観察研究のため因果推論不可。臨床実装前にvalidation・コスト評価が必要。
- Limitations: 観察研究；コホートの人種・社会経済的多様性；7,000タンパク測定の実臨床コスト；臨床実装への距離がある。
- Practice change potential: 将来的に血液1本で老化プロファイルを評価する標準検査への道を開く可能性。
- Next action: 全文でvalidation cohortの詳細・細胞型別スコアの構成タンパク質・疾患予測のAUCを確認。
- Watch keywords: plasma proteomics aging, cellular aging biomarker, Nature Medicine aging, biological age prediction
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42297981/
- OA URL: https://doi.org/10.1038/s41591-026-04446-y
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42297981/, https://doi.org/10.1038/s41591-026-04446-y
- Summary: 60,542例の血漿プロテオームから細胞型別老化スコアを機械学習で構築し、疾患予測に有用であることを示したNature Medicine掲載の大規模研究。老化の非同期性を臓器・細胞レベルで実証。血液ベースの老化評価と疾患リスク層別化への新しいアプローチ。
- Trend summary: 血液ベースの老化バイオマーカー研究が急速に進展しており、プロテオミクスによる生物学的年齢推定が疾患予測に応用される流れが加速。
- Future outlook: マルチオミクス統合や介入試験への応用、および測定コスト低下による実臨床導入が期待される。

- Deep dive reason:

- PMID: 42302891

- Population: 膝OA患者144例（平均年齢65歳、BMI30.3、64%女性）
- Intervention: DXAによる総体脂肪・内臓脂肪の定量評価

- Evidence strength: moderate
- Safety notes: 横断解析で因果不明。n=144で検出力に限界。
- Limitations: 横断解析（ベースラインデータのみ）、n=144と小規模、単施設の可能性。

- Summary: 膝OA患者144例のRCT基盤横断解析。DXAで内臓脂肪を定量し臨床アウトカムとの関連を性差別評価。男性で内臓脂肪の影響が強く、BMI超えた体組成評価の有用性を示唆。n小規模で限界あり。
- Trend summary: 肥満関連疾患でBMIを超えた体脂肪組成評価（特に内臓脂肪）と性差の重要性が注目されている。

- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42315031/
- Summary: PRISMAガイドのSRで血管外科高リスク患者191研究を評価。緩和ケア利用率の低さ・タイミングの遅さ・標準パスウェイ欠如を指摘。早期緩和ケアがICU利用減少・入院期間短縮と関連。
- Trend summary: 外科領域への早期緩和ケア統合の必要性が広く認識され、標準化パスウェイ構築の研究が増加している。
- Future outlook: 血管外科患者向けの早期緩和ケア標準パスウェイのRCTによる有効性検証が期待される。
- Deep dive: 
- Deep dive reason: 重要なSRだが、日常産科実践への直接的影響は低い。

- Trend summary: GDM早期予測バイオマーカーの探索が活発化しており、既存検査の再利用が注目されている。

- Novelty: 腸内細菌・プロバイオティクスと不妊・妊娠転帰のSR/MAとして最新の統合評価。
- Evidence strength: low
- Safety notes: プロバイオティクス製品の種類・用量が多様で一般化が難しい。免疫抑制状態での使用に注意。
- Limitations: 研究の異質性が高い；プロバイオティクス菌株・用量・期間が不均一；プラセボ効果の排除が困難。
- Practice change potential: 現時点では日常診療への大きな変化をもたらす可能性は低い。
- Next action: 全文で菌株別の効果差・妊娠率のオッズ比・エビデンスの質評価（GRADE）を確認。
- Watch keywords: probiotics IVF pregnancy outcome, gut microbiome infertility, microbiota endometrium, probiotic female fertility
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42314171/
- OA URL: 
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42314171/
- Summary: 不妊女性へのプロバイオティクス補充が臨床妊娠率をわずかに改善する可能性をObstetrics & Gynecology掲載のSR/MAで示したが、エビデンスの質は低〜中等度。患者カウンセリングの根拠として有用だが積極的推奨の根拠としては不十分。

## 44. Weight-loss drugs for adults with hypertension: a Cochrane systematic review

- Date: 2026-06-22
- Genre: ダイエット・筋トレ
- Rank: 12
- Score: 61
- Importance level: moderate
- PMID: 42316203
- DOI: 10.1002/14651858.CD015234.pub2
- Journal: Cochrane Database of Systematic Reviews
- Pub year: 2026
- Study design: Cochrane Systematic Review
- Population: 高血圧を有する肉満・肥満成人
- Intervention: 減量薬（オルリスタット・GLP-1RA・ナルトレキソン・ブプロピオン等）
- Comparison: プラセボまたは生活習慣改善のみ
- Main outcome: 血圧・体重・心血管イベント・副作用
- Key findings: 複数の減量薬が血圧を有意に低下させるが副作用プロファイルは薬剤間で異なる。GLP-1RAは心血管イベント低減に有意なデータ。Cochrane水準の証拠として補完する重要文献。
- Importance reason: CochraneレベルのSRとして最高エビデンスグレードかつ高血圧合併の肉満・肥満患者によく遇う産婦人科外来にも実用的。
- Clinical relevance: 高血圧合併肥満患者への減量薬選択と副作用カウンセリングの根拠となる。PCOS・代謝症候群を持つ女性の長期管理にも波及。
- Novelty: GLP-1RAを含む最新減量薬群を網羅したCochrane SR。
- Evidence strength: high
- Safety notes: 減量薬の血圧低下効果の一方で、達成遠慄・インスリン頭痛・消化器副作用に注意。妊娠中使用は原則禁忌。
- Limitations: RCT間の投与期間・追跡期間・イベント定義の差異；女性・少数民族のサブグループ解析は限定的。
- Practice change potential: 高血圧合併肥満へのGLP-1RA適応を支持する最高水準エビデンス。
- Next action: 全文でGLP-1RA別の血圧低下効果量・心血管イベントサブグループ・副作用比較を確認。
- Watch keywords: weight loss drug hypertension, GLP-1RA blood pressure, obesity antihypertensive, Cochrane weight management
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42316203/
- OA URL: https://doi.org/10.1002/14651858.CD015234.pub2
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42316203/, https://doi.org/10.1002/14651858.CD015234.pub2
- Summary: Cochrane SRで高血圧合併肉満・肥満成人への減量薬が血圧を有意に低下させ、GLP-1RAは心血管イベント低減にも有意なデータを示すことを示した。高血圧合併肥満へのGLP-1RA適応を支持する最高水準エビデンス。
- Trend summary: GLP-1RAの高血圧改善効果は登録若枕の考慮事項に加わりつつあり、減量・心血管両方を考慮した蓄積的エビデンスが引き続き重要。
- Future outlook: 高血圧合併肥満への専用設計RCTと、血圧降下薬とGLP-1RAの併用対分析が期待される。

- Novelty: 6つの遅延フレームワーク
- Evidence strength: moderate
- Safety notes: 難治性PPHは多職種で積極的蘇生が必要
- Limitations: レビューであり実装効果は環境依存
- Practice change potential: 高
- Next action: calibrated drape等の客観測定導入効果を追跡する
- Watch keywords: quantitative blood loss PPH, calibrated drape, PPH bundle, first response treatment
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42285120/
- OA URL: 
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42285120/, https://doi.org/10.1016/S0140-6736(26)01031-7
- Summary: PPH診断治療Lancetレビュー。目測は半数を見逃すため客観測定とバンドル対応を推奨し、避けるべき6遅延を提示。

- Summary: 27研究のメタアナリシス。妊娠前後の肝酵素上昇がGDMリスクと関連し、GGT(OR2.57)とHSI(OR2.19)が強い。異質性高・証拠確実性 very low で臨床応用は限定的。
- Trend summary: 妊娠前代謝バイオマーカーによるGDMスクリーニング精度向上の研究が拡大中。
- Future outlook: 前向き大規模コホートでの閾値最適化とスクリーニング実装効果の検証が必要。

## 58. The Texas Abortion Ban and Maternal Mental Health

- Genre: 周産期
- Rank: 2
- Score: 80
- Importance level: high
- PMID: 42313383
- DOI: 10.1001/jamanetworkopen.2026.19396
- Journal: JAMA Network Open
- Pub year: 2026
- Study design: Repeated cross-sectional study, difference-in-differences (DiD)
- Population: US mothers aged 18-49 (Texas n=4,323; non-ban states n=152,573)
- Intervention: Implementation of Texas SB8 (abortion ban, September 2021)
- Comparison: Mothers in states without abortion bans
- Main outcome: Self-reported fair or poor mental/emotional health
- Key findings: +2.52 pp increase in poor mental health post-SB8 (95%CI 0.02-5.01); largest in mothers with publicly insured children (+7.06 pp)
- Importance reason: 大規模DiD設計でAbortion政策が母体メンタルヘルスを悪化させることを示した。政策議論と周産期精神医学両面で引用される重要研究
- Clinical relevance: 政策環境が母体精神健康に与える影響を示す。日本の生殖医療・中絶政策議論の参照点
- Novelty: 国家規模サーベイを用いたDiD設計でAbortion政策の母体メンタルヘルス影響を定量化
- Evidence strength: moderate
- Safety notes: 横断反復デザインで個人追跡なし；テキサス特有の残存交絡あり
- Limitations: 横断反復デザインで因果確定は困難；テキサス固有の交絡；父親メンタルへの感度分析で有意差なく母体特異性を示唆
- Practice change potential: 中（政策・カウンセリング実践への影響大）
- Next action: 他州・他政策での類似研究と中長期追跡による因果関係確認
- Watch keywords: abortion ban maternal mental health, Texas SB8, reproductive policy mental health, Dobbs decision outcomes
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42313383/
- OA URL: 
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42313383/
- Summary: JAMA Network OpenのDiD研究。SB8後テキサス州母親の精神的不健康が+2.52 pp増加。公的保険加入児の母親で最大+7.06 pp。政策影響の重要な定量的証拠。
- Trend summary: 生殖政策と母体健康アウトカムを疫学的に評価する研究が急増。
- Future outlook: 他の禁止政策・州への一般化と長期精神健康・母子アウトカムの追跡が必要。
- Deep dive: 
- Deep dive reason: 政策研究で直接診療を変えるわけではないが重要

## 60. Association between endogenous oxytocin levels and live birth rates following fresh embryo transfer: a prospective cohort study

- Date: 2026-06-20
- Genre: 生殖
- Rank: 4
- Score: 74
- Importance level: high
- PMID: 42312200
- DOI: 10.3389/fendo.2026.1850346
- Journal: Frontiers in Endocrinology
- Pub year: 2026
- Study design: Prospective cohort
- Population: 680 infertile patients undergoing IVF cycles
- Intervention: Serum and follicular fluid oxytocin measurement
- Comparison: Levels across quartiles
- Main outcome: Live birth rate (LBR) following fresh embryo transfer
- Key findings: Each 100 pg/mL increase in serum oxytocin decreased LBR by 37% (95%CI 25-47%); follicular fluid oxytocin increase of 100 pg/mL improved LBR by 18% (95%CI 2-37%)
- Importance reason: IVF前の血清オキシトシンが生児獲得率の独立した負の予測因子であることを680例前向きコホートで示した。新規バイオマーカー候補として価値大
- Clinical relevance: IVF患者のカウンセリングやプロトコル選択における新しい予後評価指標の候補
- Novelty: 血清と卵胞液オキシトシンの方向が逆の関連を示した点は新知見
- Evidence strength: moderate
- Safety notes: 観察研究で介入なし
- Limitations: 前向きコホートだが単施設；因果関係は未確立；測定タイミングの標準化が課題
- Practice change potential: 中（バイオマーカーとしての前向き多施設検証が必要）
- Next action: 多施設前向き研究でのバイオマーカー再現性確認と閾値最適化
- Watch keywords: serum oxytocin IVF, follicular fluid oxytocin, live birth predictor ART, oxytocin metabolic syndrome IVF
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42312200/
- OA URL: https://www.frontiersin.org/journals/endocrinology/articles/10.3389/fendo.2026.1850346/pdf
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42312200/
- Summary: 680例前向きコホート。血清オキシトシン100 pg/mL増でLBR 37%低下、卵胞液オキシトシンは18%改善。血清オキシトシンはTG・LDL・インスリンと正相関しメタボリック因子との関連が示唆。
- Trend summary: IVFの予後バイオマーカー研究が血清内分泌指標の方向に拡大している。
- Future outlook: 多施設でのバイオマーカー検証と介入による転帰改善の探索が期待される。
- Deep dive: true
- Deep dive reason: 680例の前向きコホートで生児獲得率と強く関連し、IVF予後評価の新指標として実装可能性があるため

- Rank: 7
- Score: 66
- Importance level: high

- Study design: Systematic review and meta-analysis (21 RCTs, 2,656 infants)

- Practice change potential: 中（NICUプロトコルへの統合）

- Watch keywords: LISA INSURE preterm surfactant, BPD surfactant administration, less invasive surfactant, neonatal respiratory distress
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42311598/
- OA URL: https://doi.org/10.1177/30502225261453435
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42311598/
- Summary: 21RCT・2656例のメタアナリシス。LISAはINSURE比でBPD・死亡・重症IVHを低減。在胎34週以下と高ステロイド曝露例でより大きな効果を確認。
- Trend summary: LISAの有効性証拠が積み上がり低侵襲サーファクタン投与の標準化が進む。
- Future outlook: 長期神経発達と施設間普及のギャップを埋める実装研究が期待される。

## 64. Opposing effects of PM2.5 on TSH levels: effect modification by thyroid peroxidase antibody status in a preconception cohort

- Date: 2026-06-20
- Genre: 周産期
- Rank: 8
- Score: 62
- Importance level: moderate
- PMID: 42312203
- DOI: 10.3389/fendo.2026.1818739
- Journal: Frontiers in Endocrinology
- Pub year: 2026
- Study design: Prospective cohort (China Medical University Birth Cohort)
- Population: 1,357 women planning pregnancy (Liaoning, China, 2019-2023)
- Intervention: PM2.5 exposure (1-12 month windows)
- Comparison: TPOAb-positive vs TPOAb-negative subgroups
- Main outcome: TSH levels
- Key findings: 10 ug/m3 PM2.5 increase decreased TSH in TPOAb-negative (beta -0.074) but increased TSH in TPOAb-positive women (beta +0.156); interaction p=0.003; effect most pronounced at 6-month window
- Importance reason: PM2.5の甲状腺影響がTPOAb状態で方向が逆転するという新知見は環境内分泌研究の方法論に影響する
- Clinical relevance: 妊活中のTPOAb陽性女性を環境感受性サブグループとして識別する根拠の可能性
- Novelty: PM2.5×TPOAb交互作用でTSH変化の方向が逆転する現象を示した点
- Evidence strength: moderate
- Safety notes: 単一中国コホートで一般化に限界
- Limitations: 中国単一コホート；PM2.5は推定値；TSH変化の臨床的意義は未確立
- Practice change potential: 低〜中（環境内分泌研究の方法論への影響は大）
- Next action: 他コホートでのTPOAb別PM2.5影響の再現性確認
- Watch keywords: PM2.5 thyroid TSH, TPOAb PM2.5 interaction, air pollution thyroid autoimmunity, preconception thyroid environment
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42312203/
- OA URL: https://www.frontiersin.org/journals/endocrinology/articles/10.3389/fendo.2026.1818739/pdf
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42312203/
- Summary: 1357例の妊活前コホート。PM2.5増加でTPOAb陰性はTSH低下、陽性はTSH上昇と方向が逆転（交互作用p=0.003）。TPOAb陽性女性が環境感受性サブグループである可能性を示す。
- Trend summary: PM2.5の内分泌撹乱影響が個人の自己免疫㋌武用で修飾されるという研究視点が注目されている。
- Future outlook: 他コホートでの再現検証と妊娠転帰への影響評価が期待される。
- Deep dive: 
- Deep dive reason: 新規性高いが即時臨床応用には限定的

- Deep dive: 
- Deep dive reason: 体制整備研究で重要だが直接診療手技への影響は限定的

## 69. A comparison of the safety of oral labetalol versus nifedipine to manage hypertension in pregnancy in Australia: a target trial emulation

- Date: 2026-06-18
- Genre: 周産期
- Rank: 1
- Score: 88
- Importance level: critical
- PMID: 42306491
- DOI: 10.1016/j.eclinm.2026.104002
- Journal: EClinicalMedicine
- Pub year: 2026
- Study design: Target trial emulation (retrospective cohort, doubly-robust IPWRA)
- Population: 7,416妊娠例（妊娠高血圧・子癇前症・慢性高血圧）、オーストラリア・ビクトリア州2009-2020
- Intervention: ラベタロール経口（n=6,745）
- Comparison: ニフェジピン経口（n=671）
- Main outcome: 母体複合アウトカム（死亡・重篤罹患）、新生児複合アウトカム
- Key findings: ニフェジピン群で母体複合アウトカムリスク33%増加（aRR 1.33, 95%CI 1.07-1.64）。子癇・HELLP症候群・腎不全増加が主因。新生児アウトカムに有意差なし。
- Importance reason: 大規模実臨床データで妊娠高血圧の経口降圧薬安全性を比較した初の大規模ターゲットトライアルエミュレーション。ラベタロール優位の重要安全性シグナル。
- Clinical relevance: 妊娠高血圧・子癇前症の経口降圧薬選択に直結。ニフェジピン第一選択施設での処方見直しのトリガーとなりうる。
- Novelty: ターゲットトライアルエミュレーションによる7,416例規模の比較。交絡調整後もニフェジピン不良アウトカム残存が新知見。
- Evidence strength: moderate（観察研究ターゲットトライアルエミュレーション、適応バイアス残存可能性）
- Safety notes: ニフェジピン群で子癇・HELLP・腎不全増加あり。ラベタロール非承認国では代替薬選択に注意。
- Limitations: ラベタロール群に91%集中。未測定交絡残存可能性。RCTでない。
- Practice change potential: 高:ニフェジピン第一選択施設での変更検討トリガー
- Next action: 国内産婦人科ガイドラインとの照合、施設でのラベタロール使用状況確認
- Watch keywords: labetalol nifedipine pregnancy, 妊娠高血圧 降圧薬 安全性, target trial emulation obstetrics
- PubMed URL: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42306491
- OA URL: https://doi.org/10.1016/j.eclinm.2026.104002
- Source URLs: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/42306491
- Summary: オーストラリア7,416妊娠例のターゲットトライアルエミュレーション。ニフェジピン使用は母体複合アウトカムリスク33%増加。子癇・HELLP・腎不全増加が主因。新生児アウトカムに差なし。
- Trend summary: 妊娠高血圧の薬物治療比較研究は近年増加。ラベタロール優位のシグナルが蓄積しつつある。
- Future outlook: RCTによる検証が必要。国際ガイドライン更新への影響が期待される。
- Deep dive: true
- Deep dive reason: 大規模実臨床データで安全性シグナルを示し、即座に処方変更判断に影響しうる重要研究。診療ガイドラインへの影響を精査すべき。
